< review>
It is a dive bar, so don't assume it's anything other than a dive bar. The bartenders are very friendly and nice. They are quick and if they can, will always say a warm hello at the door. There is always someone busing the tables of empty glasses. They check IDs on everyone, so just take it as a compliment. There's plenty of security so I don't feel like scared or nervous of the clientele. All the patrons for the most part are just there to have fun and dance. DJ Greg is awesome. He plays all genres of music, so it can be country, hip hop, 80's, heavy metal all in one spin. So it keeps it interesting and gives you opportunity to take breaks when you don't like a song, but plenty of dancing because he's plays really great songs. But it's a good mixture of young and old. It's free and totally worth it on Friday nights.< /review>

< review>
Harmony is a super nice facility, super clean, and the service is great! There was a plastic barrier between me & my nail tech, and I wasn‚Äôt close to any other customers.

The nail tech was gentle on my cuticles and gave me a great nail shape.

Unfortunately, I was really disappointed with how my nails turned out. The biggest issue - the gel polish is SO thick, and unevenly applied, and clumpy. the pix capture the texture. I know multiple layers of polish are necessary for chrome but this result was v disappointing.

Smaller issues - The application was kind of messy so I left w nail polish all over the sides of my nails.  & I asked for a dark blue chrome look, but they turned out quite silver (different than the sample nail I picked).

and it was $50</review>

<Pictures>None< /Pictures><review>Typical Dickies/scrubs lower-end store where the shoes are wrapped in cellophane.  Prices are slightly higher than what you'd expect at a place like this, but you don't go to places like this with very high expectations.

I called before visiting to check stock for a specific style, size, and color item.  There was a bit of a language barrier, but the person on the phone was able to confirm that they had two of what I needed and agreed to set them aside.

When I visited the store the following day, it was difficult to tell who was an employee and who wasn't.  After finally finding someone, I ran into more communication issues.  After a couple of minutes and the assistance of another employee, the items were located and I purchased them.

I made the mistake of not inspecting the items (Dickies pants) before leaving the store, and unfortunately one of them was missing belt loops and improperly hemmed.   While this is clearly a manufacturer defect and not the fault of this store, I'm reticent to attempt a return after the communication issues I encountered originally.

While I would return in a pinch, this is a place I'd rather avoid.</review>< user_name>
Brandon Shoemaker</user_name>

< Text>
I am the kind of person that doesn't go the the ER until something is VERY wrong. I had to go  to the ER around 6 am on Friday due to severe food poisoning that had started around 4 am. I felt so unwell (the worst I have felt in a long time) and I knew I needed immediate attention.

I was allowed to see the doctor after 20 mins of waiting, which was not a long wait at all. My experience at the hospital started to worsen when a PA (not an RN)  did my IV ... incorrectly, may I add. I'm not sure if she pierced by vein through both sides but before I knew it my arm was overflowing in blood (you should see my arm bruise now). I remember the PA saying something along the lines of "I made a mess" (but lacking empathy for what she had done). I was feeling so unwell that I didn't have the strength to say anything except "ouch." My husband said that he couldn't see what was happening because the PA was shielding everything with her back. He said he didn't notice anything until the PA left and he saw all the blood smeared over my arm and the chair having a pool of blood (which she only roughly cleaned up). A few minutes after, she finished her shift and I felt so thankful and relieved that she was going to be gone and wouldn't have her taking care of me.

When I met the ER doctor, he didn't seemed empathetic at all and I almost felt like he thought I was faking how sick I felt because he kept asking me what my pain level was almost like he didn't believe me. Anyway, he gave me meds via IV which honestly only helped a little. However, I was still thankful to be feeling a little better. He also recommended a cocktail for my stomach and also a CT scan for my abdomen which took hours!

3-4 hours later of severe pain, nausea, discomfort, and severe dehydration. My IV bag was completely empty (despite my husband's constant reminder to the nurses to give me more IV).

An hour later, I finally received the cocktail and another hour later, I got a CT scan. And another hour later, I FINALLY got pain medication. It wasn't until this pain medication that I was finally able to rest and sleep.

If the doctor/nurses had only given me the stomach cocktail and the IV pain medication from the beginning I wouldn't have had to suffer through the pain for 5 hours straight. At some point, I was telling my husband that I'd rather just go home because I feel like I'd feel better at home than here due to the constant waiting..

I was unfortunately very disappointed in the level of health care at this facility. I hope this review can be taken seriously so no other person has to go through what I went through.<//Text>

I will preface this by saying that everyone one I came into contact with was amazing, including the Dr who gave me devastating, but false information. I was told to come back today to recheck Hcg levels.
That's were it goes wrong. My levels the first time were in the 13,000s and dropped to the 11,000s. I was told I was most likely going to lose the baby. My numbers should have risen or doubled, and the fact they went down my pregnancy was most likely not viable. I was confused and kept saying my ultrasound was fine two days ago, could I have another. I was told, very empathetically that ultrasound didnt matter. Even with heart beat, it just shows baby is where its supposed to be now, which they already know, but that it was still going to abort. He wouldn't say for sure but it was most likely. I was very upset. He went to go ask his boss (another Dr) to double check.

There was nothing they could do and he was sorry. He said they would discharge me and get my paperwork. I was so upset, I just asked to leave.  I did come back hours later to get paper work for my Obgyn.
I called and made an appointment with my Obgyn and saw them this afternoon.  They told me everything was fine. I was not losing my baby. My ob said number only rise in the first trimester and they are supposed to drop after 12 weeks.  They dont even look at hcg number after 15 weeks because they are useless.  The placenta takes over making progesterone for baby and hcg levels go down, that's why you start feeling better generally after the first trimester.  He said my numbers are within range and not to worry. The heart beat was strong cervix was closed and that was the only thing that mattered.
I don't  see how I could be told something so definitively that was so wrong. The only reason they said I was losing the baby is those numbers not doubling and I'm weeks into my second trimester.  Two Drs completely devastated me for nothing. I feel bad for the Dr who gave me the news, he really seemed upset too. It was his boss who gave the curt answer, he was just paraphrasing.  I didnt appreciate the stock market  analogy either.  I am writing this hoping someone in charge see this and can relay this information so no other pregnant woman has to get such falsely devastating news.</text>
